  "rwh_faq_a17_3" = "There are generally 3 types of filters depending on area and water quality\n1)    Sand filter: These are constructed by brick masonry and filled by pebbles, gravel, and sand. Each layer is separated by wire mesh.\n2)    Charcoal filter: Charcoal filter can be made on site or in a drum. Pebbles, gravel and sand are filled in the drum or chamber. Each layer should be separated by wire mesh. "rwh_faq_q17_200" = "2What are the different types of filters available?";
"rwh_faq_a17_200" = "2There are generally 3 types of filters depending on area and water quality\n1)    Sand filter: These are constructed by brick masonry and filled by pebbles, gravel, and sand. Each layer is separated by wire mesh.\n2)    Charcoal filter: Charcoal filter can be made on site or in a drum. Pebbles, gravel and sand are filled in the drum or chamber. Each layer should be separated by wire mesh. Thin layer of charcoal is used to absorb odour if any.\n3)    PVC pipe filter: This filter is made of PVC pipe of 1 to 1.20 m length; Diameter of pipe depends on the area of roof. Six inches dia. pipe is enough for a 1500 Sq. Ft. roof and 8 inches dia. pipe should be used for roofs more than 1500 Sq. Ft. Pipe is divided into three compartments by wire mesh.";

"rwh_faq_q20_200" = "2What happens when the rainwater tank is full?";
"rwh_faq_a20_200" = "2Underground and cellar tanks have to be fitted with an overflow through which the water can flow into the sewage system or an infiltration system. If connected to the sewage system, the overflow should be above the system\'s backed-up water level. If necessary, a backpressure flap should be installed. Above-ground tanks should always be connected to a downpipe filter. This will prevent the water from flowing inward when the rainwater tank is full and instead it will flow through the downpipe into the sewer.";
"rwh_faq_q21_200" = "2Does the rainwater collected in the rainwater tank remains fresh?";
"rwh_faq_a21_200" = "2An underground tank is ideal for storing rainwater because the soil protects the tank from light and heat. Algae and microorganisms cannot form due to exposure to sunlight and temperature, ensuring consistent water quality. If you have an above-ground rainwater tank, you must ensure that it is as opaque as possible (Not transparent or translucent) and it should installed away from direct sunlight, to prevent water from warming.";

"pc_faq_q5_200" = "2How do termites enter the house?";

Each layer is separated by wire mesh.\n2)    Charcoal filter: Charcoal filter can be made on site or in a drum. Pebbles, gravel and sand are filled in the drum or chamber. Each layer should be separated by wire mesh. Thin layer of charcoal is used to absorb odour if any.\n3)    PVC pipe filter: This filter is made of PVC pipe of 1 to 1.20 m length; Diameter of pipe depends on the area of roof. "rwh_ans19_3" = "Underground and cellar tanks have to be fitted with an overflow through which the water can flow into the sewage system or an infiltration system.
If connected to the sewage system, the overflow should be above the system's backed-up water level. If necessary, a backpressure flap should be installed. Above-ground tanks should always be connected to a downpipe filter. This will prevent the water from flowing inward when the rainwater tank is full and instead it will flow through the downpipe into the sewer.";

The worker termites enter our structure through a gap (0.5 mm gap is sufficient for them)  in search of food (cellulosic material). Material containing cellulose like wood (furniture) , paper &amp; cloth is attacked by them.";

"pc_ans3_3" = "The Principle of the treatment is To create a continuous chemical barrier / zone in between the ground and the structure so the ground nesting termites will not attack the structure";
"pc_ans4_3" = "There are 2 said treatments. Pre construction anti termite treatment - This treatment is ideal for the underconstruction buildings in its early stages. In this the chemical barrier / zone is created in the soil at plinth level and this treatment is called Pre-construction Anti-termite Treatment. And post construction anti termite treatment when the building structure is ready/existing  and infested with termites, this is done by drilling at the wall and floor junction / skirting level and creating the chemical barrier / zone at the bottom of the walls, this treatment is called Post-construction Anti-termite Treatment";

"pc_faq_q4_6" = "6What is termite (white ants, दीमक) ?";
"pc_faq_a4_6" = "6Subterranean Termites are social insects and live in colonies below ground. They are considered pests because termites enter the house structure through a gap (0.5 mm gap is sufficient) in search of food. Food for termites is household material containing cellulose like wood, wooden furniture, paper and cloth.";
"pc_faq_q5_6" = "6How do termites enter the house?";
"pc_faq_a5_6" = "6Termites need moisture to survive and spread underground. They usually enter a house from the soil through its foundation or through cracks in the slab, expansion joints, voids in brick and around plumbing. Wood structures in direct contact with the ground are also easy access routes for termites.";
"pc_faq_q6_6" = "6Can termites enter concrete?";
"pc_faq_a6_6" = "6Termites cannot pass through solid concrete, but they can get through a crack only 1/32nd of an inch wide. Openings this size or bigger often occur where two pieces of concrete abut – like when poured separately – and around plumbing penetrations through the concrete or where the concrete has cracked.";
"pc_faq_q7_6" = "6How they harm the house structure?";
"pc_faq_a7_6" = "6Termites can hollow out the wood in the structure of your house. They can also damage the inside of the walls, areas around your windows and doors and the wood furniture inside your home.";
